## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations and vibration (nonlinear dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the only state feature is velocity v, so the task most naturally fits reduced/phenomenological oscillator dynamics where acceleration is modeled as a velocity-dependent damping/drive term and/or an explicit time-dependent forcing. With only (t, v) available, common structures include nonlinear friction (in v) and non-autonomous forcing/modulation (in t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free particle / no net force: dv_dt = c0 (constant acceleration bias / gravity-like term)
- Linear relaxation / viscous drag: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v (exponential approach to a terminal velocity when c1 < 0)
- Pure linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (energy dissipation proportional to velocity)
- Quadratic (turbulent) drag: dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (drag magnitude ∝ v^2 with sign opposing motion)
- Cubic drag / higher-order damping: dv_dt = c0 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation at larger speeds)
- Mixed polynomial damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (common odd-in-v expansion for symmetric friction laws)
- Negative damping with amplitude limiting (Rayleigh-type in v): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (with c0 > 0, c1 < 0 gives self-excitation then saturation)
- Smooth Coulomb (dry) friction: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * v) (approximates sign(v) friction with differentiability)
- Sinusoidally driven damping model: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (external periodic drive plus linear damping)
- Driven with nonlinear dissipation: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (forced nonlinear oscillator reduced to velocity-only dissipation/drive)
- Parametrically modulated damping: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (time-varying effective damping/gain)
- Chirped/phase-modulated drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2 * t**2) + c3 * v (swept-frequency forcing in vibration tests)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-in-v terms (v, v**3, v**5, …) typically encode motion-reversal symmetry: dv_dt changes sign when v changes sign (common for damping/anti-damping expansions).
- A v*Abs(v) term indicates a drag force whose magnitude scales like v^2 but always opposes the direction of motion (a hallmark of quadratic/turbulent resistance).
- A tanh(c*v) dependence suggests dry friction (Coulomb friction) being smoothed for differentiability/noise robustness in fitting.
- A constant + linear term (c0 + c1*v) implies approach to a terminal velocity: dv_dt = 0 at v = -c0/c1 (stable if c1 < 0).
- A linear-plus-cubic structure (c0*v + c1*v**3) often represents self-excitation with nonlinear saturation (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|).
- Explicit sin/cos(t) terms indicate external periodic forcing; the coefficient multiplying t in the argument sets the forcing frequency scale.
- Time-dependent coefficients multiplying v, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v, suggest parametric modulation of damping/gain (e.g., time-varying environment or control).
- Including t**2 inside a sinusoid argument, sin(c1*t + c2*t**2), signals frequency sweep (chirp), common in system identification of oscillators.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
0.938430539170744\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.866974142258927\,\sin(v),
\]
i.e., **(i)** a pure \(\sin(t)\) term with constant amplitude, plus **(ii)** a pure \(\sin(v)\) term with constant amplitude, and **no** other dependence on \(t\) or \(v\) (no rational-in-\(t\) prefactors, no \(v\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), \(tv\), etc.).

A candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by choosing constants) to exactly \(A\sin(t)+B\sin(v)\) with \(A=0.9384...\), \(B=-0.8669...\).

---

### Candidates 1–4
All have a \(t\)-dependent prefactor \( \frac{c0\,t}{c3 t + c4}\sin(c1 t+c2)\) plus polynomial/odd terms in \(v\) (like \(v\), \(v|v|\), \(v^3\)) and/or \(tv/(c4+t)\).
- You can zero out the unwanted \(v\), \(v|v|\), \(v^3\), \(tv\) terms by setting their coefficients to 0.
- But the remaining \(t\)-part is **not** a constant-amplitude \(\sin(t)\) unless the prefactor is constant in \(t\). That would require \(\frac{t}{c3 t + c4}\) to be constant for all \(t\), which is impossible unless \(c4=0\) and then it becomes \(\frac{1}{c3}\) (constant) **but** the expression becomes undefined at \(t=0\) (division by 0). GT is defined at \(t=0\). So no global equivalence.
- Also none of these contain \(\sin(v)\); they only have algebraic \(v\)-terms. Those cannot equal \(-0.8669\sin(v)\) for all real \(v\).
**No match** for 1–4.

### Candidates 5–6
Contain \(c7\,v\sin(c8 t+c9)\): a product of \(v\) and a sine in \(t\), not \(\sin(v)\).
Other \(v\)-dependence is rational in \(t\) or \(tv\). You can’t turn \(v\sin(\cdot t)\) into \(\sin(v)\) by constants.
Also the \(t\)-sine term still has the problematic \(\frac{t}{c3 t+c4}\) prefactor.
**No match**.

### Candidates 7–8
Have \(v|v|\) (non-sinusoidal, and not removable unless coefficient 0) and no \(\sin(v)\).
Even if you set \(c7=0\), you still lack \(-\beta\sin(v)\).
**No match**.

### Candidates 9–12
Only linear/cubic/\(v|v|\) terms in \(v\), no \(\sin(v)\). Those cannot equal \(-0.8669\sin(v)\) for all \(v\).
Also same \(t\)-prefactor issue.
**No match**.

### Candidate 13
Has an extra \(c5/(c3 t+c4)\) and \(tv/(c3 t+c4)\) and \(v|v|\); no \(\sin(v)\).
Cannot match.
**No match**.

### Candidate 14
Has \( \exp(c1 t)\) and division by \(c4 t+c5\), plus \(v/(c4 t+c5)\) and \(v|v|\). No \(\sin(v)\).
Even setting many coefficients to 0, you cannot get a pure constant-amplitude \(\sin(t)\) without the denominator/exponential causing nontrivial \(t\)-dependence (unless you make the whole term 0).
**No match**.

### Candidate 15
Has \(\sin(\cdot t)\) divided by \(c3 t+c4\) and only algebraic \(v\)-terms (\(v/(t+\cdot)\), \(tv/(...) \), \(v|v|\)). No \(\sin(v)\).
**No match**.

### Candidate 16
\[
c0\sin(c1 t+c2)+c3 v|v|+c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(c6 v+c7).
\]
- Set \(c3=0\) to remove \(v|v|\).
- Set \(c5=0\) so \(e^{c5 t}=1\) (constant), giving \(c4\sin(c6 v+c7)\), which can match \(-0.866974...\sin(v)\) by choosing \(c6=1\), \(c7=0\), \(c4=-0.866974142258927\).
- The \(t\)-term \(c0\sin(c1 t+c2)\) can match \(0.9384305...\sin(t)\) by choosing \(c1=1\), \(c2=0\), \(c0=0.938430539170744\). (Phase-shift alternatives also possible, e.g. cosine via \(c2=\pi/2\), but not needed.)
This exactly reproduces GT with no extra terms.
**Match found (candidate 16).**

### Candidates 17–18
Only rational-in-\(t\) multiples of \(v\) and \(tv\); no \(\sin(v)\). Also \(t/(c3 t+c4)\) issue.
**No match**.

### Candidates 19, 25, 28–32, 34
These are sums of terms all divided by \((c3 t+c4)\) or similar, plus possibly constants; \(v\) appears only linearly and divided by \(t\)-dependent denominators, never as \(\sin(v)\).
Cannot produce a standalone \(-\beta\sin(v)\) term, and the \(t\)-dependence is wrong (rational/exponential structure).
**No match** for 19, 25, 28–32, 34.

### Candidates 20–24, 26–27, 29–30, 33, 35–41, 43–44
All involve \(t e^{(\cdot)t}\sin(\cdot t+\cdot)\) over \((\cdot t+\cdot)\) and \(v\) only as algebraic/rational terms, \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), or \(|v|\), but **not** \(\sin(v)\) (except none here have \(\sin(\text{linear }v)\) without extra \(t\)-factors).
Thus they cannot match the required \(-0.8669\sin(v)\) term. Also their \(t\)-part is not a pure constant-amplitude \(\sin(t)\) unless the whole term is killed.
**No match** for 20–24, 26–27, 29–30, 33, 35–41, 43–44.

### Candidates 42, 45–50
- 42: has \(v/(c3 t+c4)\), \(1/(c3 t+c4)\), and \(v^3\); no \(\sin(v)\). **No match**.
- 45: includes \(c5\sin(c6 v+c7)\) (good), but the \(t\)-sine term is \(c0\,t\sin(c1 t+c2)/(c3 t+c4)\) (bad globally as discussed), and also extra \(v/(c3 t+c4)\) and \(1/(c4+t)\) terms unless zeroed. Even if you zero extras, the \(t\)-term cannot become exactly \(0.9384\sin(t)\) for all \(t\) without introducing a singularity or nonconstant prefactor. **No match**.
- 46, 50: have \(tv\) or \(v\sin(c8 t+c9)\) products; no way to reduce to \(\sin(v)\) only. **No match**.
- 47–49: only rational \(v\) or \(v^3\) or \(v|v|\); no \(\sin(v)\). **No match**.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: [16, 45]
Matched candidates: ["c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*v*Abs(v) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*v + c7)", "c0*t*sin(c1*t + c2)/(c3*t + c4) + c5*sin(c6*v + c7) + c8*v/(c3*t + c4) + c9/(c4 + t)"]

I need to determine which candidates can exactly equal `0.938430539170744*sin(t) - 0.866974142258927*sin(v)` for all values of `t` (non-negative) and `v` (both signs).

The GT has two terms: one is a pure `sin(t)` and the other is a pure `sin(v)`. Let me analyze each candidate.

**Key observations about GT:**
- The `sin(t)` term has no dependence on `v`
- The `sin(v)` term has no dependence on `t`
- There are no polynomial terms in `v`, no `v*|v|`, no `v³`, no `v/(something with t)` terms

**For the sin(t) part:** Many candidates have `c0*t*sin(c1*t+c2)/(c3*t+c4)`. If we set `c1=1, c2=0, c3=1, c4=0`, this becomes `c0*t*sin(t)/(c3*t) = (c0/c3)*sin(t)`. So this can produce `A*sin(t)`. Similarly with `c3=0, c4≠0`: `c0*t*sin(t)/c4`, which also works. Let me use `c3=1, c4=0` giving `(c0/c3)*sin(t)`.

**For the -sin(v) part:** I need `-0.867*sin(v)`. Let me check what each candidate offers for the `v`-dependent terms.

Let me systematically check candidates that could produce `-β*sin(v)`:

**Candidates with `sin(v)` explicitly:** Only Candidate 16 and 45 have `sin()` of `v`.

**Candidate 16:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v*|v| + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*v+c7)`
- First term: `c0*sin(t)` ✓
- For sin(v): set `c5=0`, then `c4*sin(c6*v+c7)`. Set `c6=1, c7=0`: `c4*sin(v)`. Set `c3=0`.
- This gives `c0*sin(t) + c4*sin(v)` ✓

**Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 45:** `c0*t*sin(c1*t+c2)/(c3*t+c4) + c5*sin(c6*v+c7) + c8*v/(c3*t+c4) + c9/(c4+t)`
- First term → `A*sin(t)` ✓
- `c5*sin(c6*v+c7)` with `c6=1, c7=0` → `c5*sin(v)` ✓
- Need `c8=0` to kill `v/(c3*t+c4)` and `c9=0` to kill the last term.
- With `c3=1, c4=0`: `c9/(0+t) = c9/t` which must be 0, so `c9=0`. And `c8*v/(t)=0` needs `c8=0`.
- This gives `A*sin(t) + c5*sin(v)` ✓

**Candidate 45 verdict: [MATCH]**

Now let me verify all other candidates cannot match. The key issue: most candidates have `v`-dependent terms like `v`, `v*|v|`, `v³`, `v/(at+b)`, `tv/(at+b)`, `v*sin(ct+d)` — none of these equal `sin(v)`.

- Terms like `c*v`, `c*v*|v|`, `c*v³` are polynomial/piecewise in `v`, not `sin(v)`.
- `v/(c3*t+c4)` or `v/(c4+t)` are linear in `v` with `t`-dependent coefficient.
- `tv/(c3*t+c4)` similarly.
- `v*sin(c*t+d)` is `v` times a function of `t` — linear in `v`, not `sin(v)`.

None of these can produce `sin(v)`. For candidates 1-15, 17-44, 46-50 (excluding 16 and 45), the `v`-dependent terms cannot produce `-β*sin(v)`.

For candidates 19, 25, 28, 29, 31, 32, 34, 36 — these have no `v`-dependent terms at all (or only constant/t-dependent terms), so they can't match either.

After checking all candidates systematically:

Candidates 1-15, 17-44, 46-50: **[NO MATCH]** (all have wrong basis functions for the `v` dependence)
